<p><b>Lewisville</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/juː/ long 'u' in 'cute'">juː</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/./ syllable break">.</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> is a city in <a href="/wiki/Denton_County,_Texas" title="Denton County, Texas">Denton County, Texas</a>, United States. It is a northwestern suburb of <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000 United States Census</a> placed the city's population at 77,737 and the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a> placed it at 95,290, making it one of the fastest-growing city populations in the United States and the 33rd most populous in Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAasen2010_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAasen2010-6">[6]</a></sup> It occupies 36.4 square miles (94 km<sup>2</sup>) of land and includes 6.07 square miles (15.7 km<sup>2</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_Lake" title="Lewisville Lake">Lewisville Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuickFacts2015_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuickFacts2015-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Originally called Holford's Prairie, the origins of Lewisville date back to the early 1840s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECapace1999437_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECapace1999437-7">[7]</a></sup> The arrival of the town's first railroad in 1881 engendered its initial growth, and the expansion of the area's transportation infrastructure spurred further development in the early part of the 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119-8">[8]</a></sup> Lewisville <a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States" title="Local government in the United States">incorporated</a> in 1925, and when construction of Lewisville Lake was completed in the 1950s, the city began to expand rapidly.</p>
<p>Lewisville's consistently warm climate and proximity to Lewisville Lake has made it a recreational hub of the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex</a>. The city's municipal government, led by a nonpartisan city council, focuses its recreational and cultural investments on facilities such as Toyota of Lewisville Park and the MCL Grand Theater. The area's transportation infrastructure has evolved around the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I-35_Corridor" title="I-35 Corridor">I-35 Corridor</a> along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">Interstate 35E</a>. The diversity of its population and industry has created a stable economic climate. <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_Independent_School_District" title="Lewisville Independent School District">Lewisville Independent School District</a> provides most of the area's public education programs.</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1841, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a> chartered the <a href="/wiki/Peters_Colony" title="Peters Colony">Peters Colony</a> Land Grant Company (named for William Smalling Peters, publisher of the song "<a href="/wiki/Oh!_Susanna" title="Oh! Susanna">Oh! Susanna</a>")<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECapace1999437_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECapace1999437-7">[7]</a></sup> to settle the <a href="/wiki/North_Texas" title="North Texas">North Texas</a> area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1844, John W. King and his wife settled on the east side of the prairie, where the city now lies. Baptist settlers from <a href="/wiki/Platte_County,_Missouri" title="Platte County, Missouri">Platte County, Missouri</a>, settled on the west side; among them were John and James Holford, who named the area Holford's Prairie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECowling193616_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECowling193616-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates191829_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates191829-10">[10]</a></sup> Further south, Presbyterians established a church and called it <a href="/wiki/Flower_Mound,_Texas" title="Flower Mound, Texas">Flower Mound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates191831_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates191831-11">[11]</a></sup> In the confusion over land ownership after the <a href="/wiki/Hedgcoxe_War" title="Hedgcoxe War">Hedgcoxe War</a>, Basdeal Lewis purchased Holford's Prairie in 1853 and renamed it after himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20117_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20117-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1845, the Fox family, which owned about a dozen slaves, buried a slave child called Melinda on the family farm, which eventually became the town's cemetery for black residents. Named Fox–Hembry Cemetery, the plot still exists today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201148_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201148-13">[13]</a></sup> After it had fallen into disrepair, local residents and businesses gathered to restore it in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthwell2011_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthwell2011-14">[14]</a></sup> Though <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> was not on the ballot in the area for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1860" title="United States presidential election, 1860">1860 Presidential election</a>, residents of Lewisville (listed as "Hollforts" on election results) still gave <a href="/wiki/John_C._Breckinridge" title="John C. Breckinridge">John C. Breckinridge</a> only a 44–31 majority over an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fusion" title="Electoral fusion">electoral fusion</a> option.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges197894_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges197894-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era_of_the_United_States" title="Reconstruction Era of the United States">Reconstruction</a>, Lewisville became home to <a href="/wiki/Denton_County,_Texas" title="Denton County, Texas">Denton County's</a> first <a href="/wiki/Cotton_gin" title="Cotton gin">cotton gin</a>. Built in 1867, it could produce up to three bales per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates1918278_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates1918278-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges1978121_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges1978121-17">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Thirteenth_Texas_Legislature" title="Thirteenth Texas Legislature">Thirteenth Texas Legislature</a> chartered the Dallas and Wichita Railroad (later the <a href="/wiki/Missouri%E2%80%93Kansas%E2%80%93Texas_Railroad" title="Missouri–Kansas–Texas Railroad">Missouri–Kansas–Texas</a>) on terms requiring 20 miles of track to be in running order by July 1, 1875. Lewisville paid the company $15,000 to come to the city, with a promise of another $5,000 on completion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges1978147_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges1978147-18">[18]</a></sup> The company fulfilled the deal by completing the railroad tracks to a point just south of Lewisville on the morning of the deadline, and the line began running full-time in 1881.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates1918172_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates1918172-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett20119-8">[8]</a></sup> Republicans in the <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Texas_Legislature" title="Fourteenth Texas Legislature">Fourteenth Texas Legislature</a> passed a law on April 30, 1874, prohibiting alcohol within two miles of the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGammel1898595_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGammel1898595-20">[20]</a></sup> Many residents ignored the law, however, and the city retained as many as 17 saloons at one point.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBates1918146_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBates1918146-21">[21]</a></sup> The population of the unincorporated town was 500 in 1888.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoster188855_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoster188855-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Progress">Progress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Progress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg"><img alt="Photograph of an old theater sign on a rustic building." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="484" height="327" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg/220px-Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg/330px-Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg/440px-Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Theater_Old_Town.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The building currently housing the Greater Lewisville Community Theater, built in 1885, is the oldest standing structure in Lewisville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGLCT2006_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGLCT2006-23">[23]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On January 15, 1925, residents voted by a margin of 17 votes to <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">incorporate</a> Lewisville, which established its official boundaries as a city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHervey200226_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHervey200226-2">[2]</a></sup> By 1930, Lewisville's population had increased to 853, making it the fourth most populous municipality in Denton County (behind <a href="/wiki/Denton,_Texas" title="Denton, Texas">Denton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanger,_Texas" title="Sanger, Texas">Sanger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pilot_Point,_Texas" title="Pilot Point, Texas">Pilot Point</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges1978367_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges1978367-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because the city's economy had become diversified before the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a>, Lewisville was relatively well insulated from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. Many residents, including business leaders, nevertheless supported the <a href="/wiki/New_Deal" title="New Deal">New Deal</a> programs of <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201125_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201125-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDegan199121.E2.80.9323_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDegan199121.E2.80.9323-26">[26]</a></sup> By 1936, the <a href="/wiki/Works_Progress_Administration" title="Works Progress Administration">Works Progress Administration</a> operated a cannery in the city to provide temporary jobs for unemployed residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges1978371_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges1978371-27">[27]</a></sup> As an extension of the <a href="/wiki/Good_Roads_Movement" title="Good Roads Movement">Good Roads Movement</a>, which had been prominent in Denton County since the early 1910s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlmanac1912279_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlmanac1912279-28">[28]</a></sup> residents formed the Good Roads Committee of Lewisville to lobby state and federal officials for funding to create better streets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201127.E2.80.9332_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201127.E2.80.9332-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBridges1978287_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBridges1978287-30">[30]</a></sup> Lewisville celebrated the paving of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_77_in_Texas" title="U.S. Route 77 in Texas">U.S. Route 77</a> between Denton and <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> in 1931 with a "Coming Out of the Mud" ceremony. The new pavement closed the "Lewisville Gap" between the two cities, a stretch of dirt road through the city that often became too muddy for travel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOdom199669_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOdom199669-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The new road also led indirectly to the downfall of the area's public transportation system. Between 1925 and 1932, the Texas Interurban Railway, an electric <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a> service that ran from Dallas to Denton, operated a station in Lewisville. Business leaders in the Lewisville Chamber of Commerce welcomed the service at the time, proudly citing the city's <a href="/wiki/Progressivism_in_the_United_States" title="Progressivism in the United States">progressive</a> citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETunnellMooreMinor192515_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETunnellMooreMinor192515-32">[32]</a></sup> The area's low population density could not sustain the venture, however, and in 1932, the line went out of business and immediately halted service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoynihan20076_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoynihan20076-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECochran199215_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECochran199215-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 25, 1934, <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Hamilton" title="Raymond Hamilton">Raymond Hamilton</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Gang" title="Barrow Gang">Barrow Gang</a> robbed the First National Bank of Lewisville. Residents chased him to <a href="/wiki/Howe,_Texas" title="Howe, Texas">Howe, Texas</a>, where he was captured at a roadblock and transferred to Dallas County Jail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201152_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201152-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERiddell1934_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERiddell1934-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth">Growth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Growth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lewisville's rapid growth began when construction of the Garza–Little Elm Dam finished in 1954, expanding the Garza–Little Elm Reservoir into the what is now <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_Lake" title="Lewisville Lake">Lewisville Lake</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201199_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett201199-37">[37]</a></sup> The city adopted a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Rule_in_the_United_States" title="Home Rule in the United States">home rule</a> charter for a <a href="/wiki/Council%E2%80%93manager_government" title="Council–manager government">council–manager</a> style of municipal government in 1963, becoming one of only a few home rule cities in Texas with a population of less than 5,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAlmanac1964553.E2.80.93554_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlmanac1964553.E2.80.93554-38">[38]</a></sup> In September 1969, 13 days after <a href="/wiki/Woodstock" title="Woodstock">Woodstock</a>, the city hosted the <a href="/wiki/Texas_International_Pop_Festival" title="Texas International Pop Festival">Texas International Pop Festival</a>, which drew over 150,000 spectators and featured performances by <a href="/wiki/Janis_Joplin" title="Janis Joplin">Janis Joplin</a>, <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">Led Zeppelin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilonsky2011_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilonsky2011-39">[39]</a></sup> In 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Historical_Commission" title="Texas Historical Commission">Texas Historical Commission</a> dedicated a historical event marker at the <a href="/wiki/Hebron_(DCTA_station)" title="Hebron (DCTA station)">Hebron</a> <a href="/wiki/A-train_(Denton_County_Transportation_Authority)" title="A-train (Denton County Transportation Authority)">A-train</a> station in Lewisville to commemorate the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2011_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2011-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>When <a href="/wiki/Dallas/Fort_Worth_International_Airport" title="Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport">Dallas/Fort Worth International Airport</a> opened to the south of the city in 1974 and <a href="/wiki/Vista_Ridge_Mall" title="Vista Ridge Mall">Vista Ridge Mall</a> opened at the intersection of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35E_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35E (Texas)">Interstate 35E</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FM_3040" title="FM 3040">Round Grove Road</a> in 1989, Lewisville began to undergo rapid suburban growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011125_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011125-41">[41]</a></sup> Its population increased from 24,273 in 1980 to 46,521 in 1990, making it the 40th most populous city in Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiskura199095_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiskura199095-42">[42]</a></sup> In the early 1990s, the Lewisville Chamber of Commerce marketed the city with the slogan "City of Expanding Horizons".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewisville_COC1991136_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewisville_COC1991136-43">[43]</a></sup> The population reached 77,737 in 2000 and 95,290 in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQuickFacts2015_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQuickFacts2015-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lewisville is located at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Lewisville%2C_Texas&amp;params=33_2_18_N_97_0_22_W_type:city"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">33°2′18″N</span> <span class="longitude">97°0′22″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">33.03833°N 97.00611°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">33.03833; -97.00611</span></span></span></a></span> (33.038316, −97.006232)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011-44">[44]</a></sup> at an elevation of about 550 feet (170 m). It has a total area of 42.47 square miles (110.0 km<sup>2</sup>), of which 36.4 sq mi (94 km<sup>2</sup>) is land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011-44">[44]</a></sup> It lies at the southern end of Denton County and the northern end of the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex</a>, in the eastern part of the <a href="/wiki/Cross_Timbers" title="Cross Timbers">Cross Timbers</a> region of Texas between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_Blackland_Prairies" title="Texas Blackland Prairies">Texas Blackland Prairies</a> and the Grand Prairie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECapace1999437_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECapace1999437-7">[7]</a></sup> Vista Ridge, a small plateau, is in the southeast corner of Lewisville, and the lowest part of Denton County, at 484 feet (148 m), is found in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECowling193662_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECowling193662-45">[45]</a></sup> Lewisville sits above the <a href="/wiki/Barnett_Shale" title="Barnett Shale">Barnett Shale</a>, a geological formation containing a large quantity of <a href="/wiki/Shale_gas_in_the_United_States" title="Shale gas in the United States">natural shale gas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHundley2011a_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHundley2011a-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>Water constitutes 6.072 sq mi (15.73 km<sup>2</sup>) of the city's total area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGazetteer2011-44">[44]</a></sup> including Lewisville Lake, the Elm Fork of the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_River_(Texas)" title="Trinity River (Texas)">Trinity River</a>, and two local tributaries of the Elm Fork, Prairie Creek and Timber Creek. A <a href="/wiki/Riparian_zone" title="Riparian zone">riparian zone</a> encompasses a portion of the city in the southeast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESales20076_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESales20076-47">[47]</a></sup> The intersection of the Elm Fork and Lake Lewisville has given rise to a <a href="/wiki/River_delta" title="River delta">delta</a> at the southern end of the lake, extending 6.9 miles (11.1 km) south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliams1991_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliams1991-48">[48]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> has labeled much of the area surrounding the delta as "Zone AE", meaning that the area is subject to <a href="/wiki/100-year_flood" title="100-year flood">100-year flood</a> precautions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFEMA2011_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFEMA2011-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_weather">Climate and weather</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate and weather">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lewisville's climate is classified as <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> is <i>Cfa</i>, which means that it has a temperate climate, does not have a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a>, and has a hot summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeelFinlaysonMcMahon20071636_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeelFinlaysonMcMahon20071636-50">[50]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Agriculture" title="United States Department of Agriculture">United States Department of Agriculture</a>, Lewisville is located in a <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">hardiness zone</a> of 8a.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUSDA2012_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUSDA2012-51">[51]</a></sup> The city is seldom affected by <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carla" title="Hurricane Carla">Hurricane Carla</a> in 1961 brought 86-mile-per-hour (138 km/h) winds and caused 6-foot (1.8 m) swells on Lewisville Lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011109_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011109-52">[52]</a></sup> During heavy rains, Timber Creek can overflow its banks, and on rare occasion, flood some of the surrounding homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStoler2010_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStoler2010-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Weather_Service" title="National Weather Service">National Weather Service</a> defines no official borders for <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>, but Lewisville is considered to be in it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENCDC2012_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENCDC2012-54">[54]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_cultural_life">Arts and cultural life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Arts and cultural life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MCL_Grand_Theater">MCL Grand Theater</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: MCL Grand Theater">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MCL_Theater.png"><img alt='A nighttime photograph of a building that says "Grand Theater" across the front.' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2520" data-file-width="3842" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/MCL_Theater.png/220px-MCL_Theater.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/MCL_Theater.png/330px-MCL_Theater.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/MCL_Theater.png/440px-MCL_Theater.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MCL_Theater.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Medical Center of Lewisville Grand Theater, which opened in 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011a_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011a-56">[56]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Medical Center of Lewisville Grand Theater, known informally as the MCL Grand, is located on the east side of Interstate 35E in Lewisville's Old Town. It functions as a hub for the arts in Lewisville, able to show films, host meetings, and provide a venue for various kinds of artistic performance. The project began in 2004 and aimed to fulfill a long-term goal of building an arts center to coincide with the 2011 opening of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_(DCTA_station)" title="Old Town (DCTA station)">Old Town Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011b_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011b-57">[57]</a></sup> The facility opened in January 2011 with a series of performances, children's shows, concerts, and exhibits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011a_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011a-56">[56]</a></sup> and the Greater Lewisville Arts Alliance presented the theater with a $25,000 contribution to begin their fundraiser to place a <a href="/wiki/Steinway_%26_Sons" title="Steinway &amp; Sons">Steinway</a> piano in the theater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011d_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011d-58">[58]</a></sup> In 2011 and 2012, <i>The Flower Mound Connection</i> newspaper named the MCL Grand the best events venue in Denton County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERodriguez2011_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERodriguez2011-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen2012_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen2012-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg"><img alt="The entrance of a building with a glass front." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="800" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg/220px-Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg/330px-Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg/440px-Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Public_Library.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Front of the Lewisville Public Library building, which opened in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city government created the Lewisville Public Library in 1968, naming Cindy Bennett as its first director. A 5,000 sq ft (460 m<sup>2</sup>) structure was built where the city hall now stands. A new library facility was built in 1986 as part of the municipal building on Main Street. In 2001, Lewisville voters approved a 4B tax package, part of which was dedicated to building a new library facility,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEaken2008_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEaken2008-61">[61]</a></sup> the children's wing of which was dedicated to Bennett.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEaken2009_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEaken2009-62">[62]</a></sup> The $11 million renovation opened in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHixson2006_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHixson2006-63">[63]</a></sup> and it received the Achievement of Excellence in Libraries Award in that year and again in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2010a_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2010a-64">[64]</a></sup> Lewisville was also the temporary home of the <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush_Presidential_Center" title="George W. Bush Presidential Center">George W. Bush Presidential Library</a> until 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGinsbergLunder20103_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGinsbergLunder20103-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEYip2013_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYip2013-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lewisville is served mainly by media from the Dallas area, but a number of niche publications focus on local news. <i>The Lewisville Enterprise</i> merged with <i>The Lewisville Leader</i> in 1962. The paper's publisher and editor at the time, U.O. Clements, was a staunch conservative, but vociferously supported the racial integration of <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_Independent_School_District" title="Lewisville Independent School District">Lewisville Independent School District</a>, for which he received many anonymous threats from members of the <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPareti200040.E2.80.9346_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPareti200040.E2.80.9346-67">[67]</a></sup> Clements sold the paper to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harte-Hanks" title="Harte-Hanks">Harte-Hanks Community Newspapers</a> in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPareti200050_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPareti200050-68">[68]</a></sup> Star Newspapers, which owned the <i>Leader</i>, was purchased by 1013 Communications in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMann2012_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMann2012-69">[69]</a></sup> The newspaper is based in <a href="/wiki/Plano,_Texas" title="Plano, Texas">Plano, Texas</a>. In 2011, the Lewisville City Council designated the Lewisville portion of <i><a href="/wiki/Neighborsgo" title="Neighborsgo">Neighborsgo</a></i>, a weekly section of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dallas_Morning_News" title="The Dallas Morning News">The Dallas Morning News</a></i>, as the city's official newspaper of record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinze2011b_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinze2011b-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:490px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv/490px--A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:490px;height:360px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="6.6066" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville,_Texas.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/93/A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv/A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="490" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="584016" data-framerate="29.97002997003"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/93/A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv/A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville%2C_Texas.ogv.360p.ogv" type="video/ogg; <div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_day_skating_at_Scion_Skate_Park_in_Lewisville,_Texas.ogv" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skateboarders at Scion Skate Park in Toyota of Lewisville Railroad Park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The City of Lewisville operates various public recreation facilities, including parks, two recreation centers, and approximately 14 miles (23 km) of trails.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughesWoodWitte201164_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughesWoodWitte201164-71">[71]</a></sup> The $20 million Railroad Park was built in 2009 using the revenue from a quarter-cent sales tax increase; it was the largest capital project in the city's history at the time. It was renamed Toyota of Lewisville Railroad Park in 2010 in a deal worth $1.5 million. The park has a baseball/softball complex, a football complex, eight lighted soccer fields, two concession buildings, a perimeter walking/jogging trail, three man-made lakes, a <a href="/wiki/Dog_park" title="Dog park">dog park</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scion_(automobile)" title="Scion (automobile)">Scion</a> <a href="/wiki/Skatepark" title="Skatepark">Skate Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmith2010b_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith2010b-72">[72]</a></sup> Since 2010, the skate park has hosted the Scion Regional Amateur Tour, part an annual series of six skateboarding competitions held across the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESkateboarder2011_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESkateboarder2011-73">[73]</a></sup> In 2012, the venue hosted its first annual <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> event benefiting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_Appointed_Special_Advocates" title="Court Appointed Special Advocates">Court Appointed Special Advocates</a> (CASA) of Denton County.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2012-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lewisville Lake Park comprises 662 acres (268 ha), which the city leases from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers" title="United States Army Corps of Engineers">United States Army Corps of Engineers</a>. The park includes various amenities, including athletic fields and designated campgrounds. The Lewisville Fishing Barge, an indoor–outdoor fishing facility that opened in 1958, is located on the lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011109_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECole-Jett2011109-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcQuarrie1988209_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcQuarrie1988209-75">[75]</a></sup> The park also hosts the Rick Neill Memorial, a cross country running meet organized each year by the <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_High_School" title="Lewisville High School">Lewisville High School</a> track and field team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomas2010_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomas2010-76">[76]</a></sup> In February 2013, the city began to review a development proposal to build a resort hotel and convention center on a 60-acre (0.24 km<sup>2</sup>) parcel of land next to the lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHundley2013_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHundley2013-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lewisville is also a major hub of the Northern Golf Corridor of the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolland2001_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolland2001-78">[78]</a></sup> Golf facilities located in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Hank_Haney" title="Hank Haney">Hank Haney</a> Golf Ranch at Vista Ridge and Timbercreek Golf Center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDodson20108_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDodson20108-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMendez2004_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMendez2004-80">[80]</a></sup> Located on the southeast edge of the city, the Lakes at Castle Hills is a <a href="/wiki/Jay_Morrish" title="Jay Morrish">Jay Morrish</a>-designed course which opened in the late 1990s; critics have rated the course highly, praising its amenities and difficulty level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcWilliams200568.E2.80.9369_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcWilliams200568.E2.80.9369-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolland2001_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolland2001-78">[78]</a></sup> Lake Park Golf Course, located near Lewisville Lake, is noted for its beginner-friendly design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcWilliams200596.E2.80.9397_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcWilliams200596.E2.80.9397-82">[82]</a></sup> The nine-hole, 1,724-yard (1,576 m) Lake Park Executive course opened in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGolf_Texas2012_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGolf_Texas2012-83">[83]</a></sup> Lewisville is also home to professional golfer <a href="/wiki/Chad_Campbell" title="Chad Campbell">Chad Campbell</a>, winner of the 2003 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Tour_Championship" title="The Tour Championship">Tour Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEValianteStachura2005_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEValianteStachura2005-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, the Lewisville Park Board proposed a new master plan for the city's parks and recreation facilities. It specifies a major overhaul of the city's trail system, including 51 miles (82 km) of off-street trails, 50 miles (80 km) of enhanced sidewalks, 50 miles (80 km) of bicycle routes, a 7.4-mile (11.9 km) paddling trail down the Elm Fork of the Trinity River, and 31 major and minor trailheads throughout the area, many of which would connect to other trail networks. The plan includes numerous crossings of Interstate 35E for pedestrian and bicyclist safety.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHughesWoodWitte201173.E2.80.9392_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHughesWoodWitte201173.E2.80.9392-85">[85]</a></sup> In March 2012, the Park Board began reviewing a new master plan to address the next ten years of park development in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELundy2012_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELundy2012-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville,_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png"><img alt="A box beam from the World Trade Center South Tower on display at the Lewisville Fire Department offices as a memorial to the service members who died as a result of the September 11 attacks" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1619" data-file-width="1351" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png/220px-Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png/330px-Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png/440px-Lewisville%2C_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville,_Texas_Fire_Department_September_11th_Memorial.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Box_beam" title="Box beam">box beam</a> from the World Trade Center <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tenants_in_Two_World_Trade_Center" title="List of tenants in Two World Trade Center">South Tower</a> stands on display in front of the Lewisville Fire Department offices as a memorial to those who died as a result of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since 1963, the City of Lewisville has operated as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Home_Rule_in_the_United_States" title="Home Rule in the United States">home rule</a> city with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Council-manager_government" title="Council-manager government">council–manager</a> style of municipal government. Residents elect six <a href="/wiki/At-large" title="At-large">at-large</a> members to serve on the City Council, including a mayor. Council elections in Texas are nonpartisan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrownLangeneggerGarc.C3.ADaLewis201199_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrownLangeneggerGarc.C3.ADaLewis201199-87">[87]</a></sup> Members are elected to three-year terms and are not term-limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHeinze2011a_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHeinze2011a-88">[88]</a></sup> The mayor does not vote on issues that come before the council except in the case of a tie. There were three different female mayors between 1985 and 2000, but no woman has served on the City Council since 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011c_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011c-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2011, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fitch_Group" title="Fitch Group">Fitch Group</a> upgraded the city's <a href="/wiki/General_obligation_bond" title="General obligation bond">general obligation bond</a> rating from "AA+" to "AAA".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFitch2011_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFitch2011-90">[90]</a></sup> Lewisville has the lowest municipal property tax rate in the Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESharp201095_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharp201095-91">[91]</a></sup> In the fiscal year 2012–2013, the city government's operating funds totaled $124,845,436.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarron2015117_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarron2015117-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Lewisville Police Department had 27 sworn police officers in 1977, and the number had increased to 136 by 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurgess20071356_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurgess20071356-93">[93]</a></sup> As of 2015, the department included 229 full-time employees, four of whom were administrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarron2015208_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarron2015208-94">[94]</a></sup> The Lewisville Fire Department included 146 full-time employees, six of whom were administrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarron2015221_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarron2015221-95">[95]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, the fire department and its then chief, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Lasky" title="Rick Lasky">Rick Lasky</a>, attracted national attention when they raised a large amount of donations for victims' families. As a reward, <a href="/wiki/John_Travolta" title="John Travolta">John Travolta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joaquin_Phoenix" title="Joaquin Phoenix">Joaquin Phoenix</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Patrick" title="Robert Patrick">Robert Patrick</a> visited the department in 2004 to promote the release of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Ladder_49" title="Ladder 49">Ladder 49</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFire2009_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFire2009-96">[96]</a></sup> In May 2011, Lewisville residents approved a sales tax increase to create two public safety districts. The revenue from the increase will fund investments in the city's police and fire departments, including new officers and vehicles, as well as a new fire station in the eastern part of the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011e_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGoodwin2011e-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lewisville is located in the <a href="/wiki/Texas%27s_26th_congressional_district" title="Texas's 26th congressional district">26th Congressional district</a> in Texas, which is represented in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a> by <a href="/wiki/Michael_C._Burgess" title="Michael C. Burgess">Michael C. Burgess</a>. As of 2015, the city is represented in <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate,_District_12" title="Texas Senate, District 12">District 12</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Senate" title="Texas Senate">Texas Senate</a> by <a href="/wiki/Jane_Nelson" title="Jane Nelson">Jane Nelson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETXmap2012a_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETXmap2012a-98">[98]</a></sup> The city is split between two <a href="/wiki/Texas_House_of_Representatives" title="Texas House of Representatives">Texas House of Representatives</a> districts: <a href="/wiki/Texas_House_of_Representatives,_District_63" title="Texas House of Representatives, District 63">District 63</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Tan_Parker" title="Tan Parker">Tan Parker</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Texas_House_of_Representatives,_District_65" title="Texas House of Representatives, District 65">District 65</a>, represented by Ron Simmons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETXmap2012b_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETXmap2012b-99">[99]</a></sup> Lewisville is a voluntary member of the <a href="/wiki/North_Central_Texas_Council_of_Governments" title="North Central Texas Council of Governments">North Central Texas Council of Governments</a>, the purpose of which is to coordinate individual and collective local governments and facilitate regional solutions, eliminate unnecessary duplication, and enable joint decisions.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg"><img alt="Photograph of a commuter rail stop." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2608" data-file-width="3880" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg/220px-Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg/330px-Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg/440px-Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lewisville_Old_Town_DCTA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The A-train station in Old Town Lewisville, opened in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The primary freeway running through Lewisville is Interstate 35E, which runs north–south through the city. Before it was built, US Highway 77 (now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farm_to_Market_Road_3504" title="Farm to Market Road 3504">Mill Street</a>) was the main through route, connecting the city with Denton to the north and Dallas to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOdom199669_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOdom199669-31">[31]</a></sup> In 1998, the <a href="/wiki/Texas_Department_of_Transportation" title="Texas Department of Transportation">Texas Department of Transportation</a> carried out a <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_the_United_States#Funding" title="Transportation in the United States">Major Investment Study</a> to examine the possibility of expanding the section of Interstate 35E between <a href="/wiki/Interstate_635_(Texas)" title="Interstate 635 (Texas)">Interstate 635</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_380" title="U.S. Route 380">U.S. Route 380</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESingh2013_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESingh2013-100">[100]</a></sup> the primary focus being an 8-mile (13 km) stretch from <a href="/wiki/Texas_State_Highway_121" title="Texas State Highway 121">Texas State Highway 121</a> to the bridge crossing Lewisville Lake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReinecke201210_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReinecke201210-101">[101]</a></sup> The project is scheduled to add one general-purpose lane in each direction, in addition to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_occupancy/toll_and_express_toll_lanes" title="High occupancy/toll and express toll lanes">managed toll lane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELewis2012_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELewis2012-102">[102]</a></sup> The project is expected to allow the city to substantially renovate its portion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I-35_Corridor" title="I-35 Corridor">I-35 Corridor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHundley2011c_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHundley2011c-103">[103]</a></sup> Construction on the first phase of the project is projected to begin in summer 2013 and finish in late 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBenning2012_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBenning2012-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>Texas State Highway 121, which runs along the <a href="/wiki/Sam_Rayburn_Tollway" title="Sam Rayburn Tollway">Sam Rayburn Tollway</a>, intersects with Interstate 35E in the southeastern edge of the city. <a href="/wiki/Farm_to_Market_Road_1171" title="Farm to Market Road 1171">Farm to Market Road 1171</a>, known in the city as Main Street, runs east–west across the middle part of the city from <a href="/wiki/Business_route" title="Business route">Business Highway 121</a> to <a href="/wiki/Interstate_35W_(Texas)" title="Interstate 35W (Texas)">Interstate 35W</a>. <a href="/wiki/Farm_to_Market_Road_407" title="Farm to Market Road 407">Farm to Market Road 407</a> runs east–west across the northern part of the city. Lewisville also encompasses most of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farm_to_Market_Road_3040" title="Farm to Market Road 3040">Farm to Market Road 3040</a>, which runs east–west towards <a href="/wiki/Carrollton,_Texas" title="Carrollton, Texas">Carrollton</a> and Flower Mound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMap_Book2010_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMap_Book2010-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lewisville residents voted in a special election held on September 13, 2003, to become a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Denton_County_Transportation_Authority" title="Denton County Transportation Authority">Denton County Transportation Authority</a> (DCTA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPhillips2003_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPhillips2003-106">[106]</a></sup> The authority began running a regional bus service in November 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPry2006_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPry2006-107">[107]</a></sup> In 2011, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Town_Station" title="Old Town Station">Old Town</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hebron_Station" title="Hebron Station">Hebron</a> stations opened as commuter stops along the route of the DCTA's <a href="/wiki/A-train_(Denton_County_Transportation_Authority)" title="A-train (Denton County Transportation Authority)">A-train</a>. The route continues north to Denton and south to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_Mills_Station" title="Trinity Mills Station">Trinity Mills Station</a> in Carrollton, where it connects with the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Area_Rapid_Transit" title="Dallas Area Rapid Transit">Dallas Area Rapid Transit</a> (DART) <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(Dallas_Area_Rapid_Transit)" title="Green Line (Dallas Area Rapid Transit)">Green Line</a> to Dallas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHundley2011b_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHundley2011b-108">[108]</a></sup> DCTA also owns a Rail Operation and Maintenance Facility in Lewisville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESouthwell2012_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESouthwell2012-109">[109]</a></sup></p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a> recorded a population of 95,290 in Lewisville, up from the 77,737 recorded for the <a href="/wiki/2000_United_States_Census" title="2000 United States Census">2000 Census</a>, making it one of the 25 fastest-growing city populations in the United States. The 2010 population was made up of 37,496 households and 23,417 families. Its <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census" title="Race and ethnicity in the United States Census">racial makeup</a> was 65.3% White, 11.2% African American, 0.7% Native American, 7.8% Asian, 11.3% from other races, and 3.2% from two or more races. 29.2% of the population was considered to be of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_(U.S._Census)" title="Hispanic (U.S. Census)">Hispanic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latino_(U.S._Census)" title="Latino (U.S. Census)">Latino</a> origin. There were children under the age of 18 in 35.5% of the households. The average household size was 2.53 persons and the average family size was 3.21 persons. The median age was 30.9 years. Between 2007 and 2011, the median income for a Lewisville household was $56,811, and per capita income was $28,144. About 9.6% of the population was below the poverty line, as compared to 17% for Texas as a whole.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The city has a diverse commercial tax base. Its top employers include <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>, Lewisville Independent School District, and <a href="/wiki/Nationstar_Mortgage" title="Nationstar Mortgage">Nationstar Mortgage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKingMartin2013203_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKingMartin2013203-112">[112]</a></sup> Automobile dealerships have flourished there, including Huffines Auto Dealerships and Village Auto Group, which was ranked as one of the top "Powerhouses of the New Economy" by <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Enterprise" title="Black Enterprise">Black Enterprise</a></i> magazine in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGite2000149_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGite2000149-113">[113]</a></sup> Lewisville's lake and the city's location in the DFW Metroplex has contributed to the largest boat sales market in the state by volume in a state that is second in the nation in overall boat sales. Because of the city's proximity to Dallas and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Worth,_Texas" title="Fort Worth, Texas">Fort Worth</a>, a number of food distribution companies have branches in Lewisville, including <a href="/wiki/Sysco" title="Sysco">Sysco</a> and Meadowbrook Meat Company (MBM). <a href="/wiki/Core-Mark#Fleming_Companies" title="Core-Mark">Fleming Companies</a>, one of the United States' largest food distribution companies, relocated to Lewisville in 2000, but it filed for <a href="/wiki/Chapter_11,_Title_11,_United_States_Code" title="Chapter 11, Title 11, United States Code">Chapter 11 bankruptcy</a> in 2003 after the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a> announced that the company had been hiding massive losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarkham2006374_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkham2006374-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Responsive_Education_Solutions" title="Responsive Education Solutions">Responsive Education Solutions</a>, which operates chartered schools nationwide, is also headquartered in Lewisville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELane2014_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELane2014-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lewisville,_Texas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<th colspan="4">Source: U.S. Census Bureau, 2007–2011 American Community Survey<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEACS2011_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEACS2011-116">[116]</a></sup></th>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lewisville_Independent_School_District" title="Lewisville Independent School District">Lewisville Independent School District</a> operates the area's public school system, including <a href="/wiki/Lewisville_High_School" title="Lewisville High School">Lewisville High School</a>. Four of the district's middle schools feed into two high school feeder campuses; since the 2011–2012 school year, the <a href="/wiki/Killough_Lewisville_High_School_North" title="Killough Lewisville High School North">Killough</a> and Harmon campuses have served the city's ninth and tenth grade students, while the main campus at the intersection of FM 1171 (Main Street) and Valley Parkway is used primarily for eleventh and twelfth grade students.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlores2012_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlores2012-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPlunkett2012_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPlunkett2012-118">[118]</a></sup> The district also operates the <a href="/wiki/Dale_Jackson_Career_Center" title="Dale Jackson Career Center">Dale Jackson Career Center</a> and conducts a night high school in Lewisville.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELISD2012_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELISD2012-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/American_Community_Survey" title="American Community Survey">American Community Survey</a> results from 2007 to 2011, 86.7% of the city's population aged 25 or older had graduated from high school, 29.7% held a bachelor's degree or higher, and 8.4% held a graduate or professional degree. The survey estimated that 24,879 Lewisville residents over the age of three were enrolled in schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEACS2011_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEACS2011-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
